                                COMPOSITE SCHEME OF ARRANGEMENT
Details of the Scheme of Arrangement
The Scheme of Arrangement filed under Sections 230 to 232 and other applicable provisions of the Companies Act, 2013 inter
alia involves:
(i) demerger, transfer and vesting of the Demerged Undertaking (as defined hereinafter), comprising of the Commercial
    Vehicles Business, from the Demerged Company into the Resulting Company on a going concern basis, and issue of shares
    by the Resulting Company to the shareholders of the Demerged Company, in accordance with Share Entitlement Ratio
    (as defined hereinafter) in consideration thereof, in accordance with the provisions of Section 2(19AA) and other relevant
    provisions of the Income Tax Act 1961; and
(ii) amalgamation of the Amalgamating Company with the Amalgamated Company with an objective of consolidating the
     Passenger Vehicles Business with the Amalgamated Company in accordance with the provisions of Section 2(1B) and other
     relevant provisions of the Income Tax Act and consequent dissolution of the Amalgamating Company without being wound
     up; and
(iii) various other matters consequential or otherwise integrally connected therewith in the manner set out in the Scheme.
Rationale for the Scheme of Arrangement
The Scheme was proposed to segregate the Commercial Vehicle Business from the Passenger Vehicles Business of the Demerged
Company and demerge it into the Resulting Company.
The effectiveness of the Scheme would result in creation of two listed companies, forming part of the Tata Group, with identical
shareholding (including common promoters) with the Resulting Company housing the Commercial Vehicles Business and the
Amalgamated Company housing the Passenger Vehicles Business. This will empower the respective businesses to pursue their
respective strategies to deliver higher growth with greater agility while reinforcing accountability.
The Scheme is in the best interests of the Companies and their respective shareholders, employees, creditors and other
stakeholders for the following reasons:
(i) The distinctive profile and established business model of the Commercial Vehicles Business and Passenger Vehicles
    Business makes it suitable to be housed in separately listed entities, allowing sharper strategic focus in pursuit of their
    independent value creation trajectories;
(ii) The Scheme would result in better and efficient control and management for the Commercial Vehicles Business and the
     Passenger Vehicles Business and would further empower the respective businesses to pursue their respective strategies to
     deliver growth with greater agility while reinforcing accountability;
(iii) The Scheme would unlock value for the overall-business portfolio through price-discovery of the Amalgamated Company
      and the Resulting Company for existing shareholders and shall entail direct holding of marketable securities therein;
(iv) The Scheme could lead to the right operating architecture for both companies with sharper focus on their individual
     business strategies and clear capital allocation, in alignment with their respective value creation journeys; and
(v) Separately listed companies will attract specific set of investors for their business profile, and consequently, encourage
    focused capital market outcomes.
Unless otherwise defined, capitalised terms used but not defined in this section shall have the same meaning assigned to such
terms in the Scheme.
Appointed Date and Effective Date
The Scheme has become effective on October 1, 2025, from the Appointed Date.
In terms of the Scheme “Appointed Date” means opening business hours of 1st July 2025 and the “Effective Date” means date
on which the last of the approvals or events specified in Clause 44 of the Scheme are satisfied or have occurred or obtained or
the requirement of which have been waived (in writing) in accordance with the Scheme.
The NCLT, through its order dated August 25, 2025 read along with rectification order dated September 10, 2025 (certified copy
of the order was received on September 25, 2025), sanctioned the Scheme.
Accordingly, the board of directors of Tata Motors Limited, Tata Motors Passenger Vehicles Limited and the Company have, at
their meeting held on September 26, 2025 mutually acknowledged that all the conditions specified in Clause 44 of the Scheme
have been fulfilled and satisfied, and accordingly, decided to keep the Effective Date of the Scheme as 1st October 2025, in
accordance with the terms of the Scheme.



                                                              65
Key Features of the Scheme (as more particularly described in the Scheme)
Key clauses of the Scheme that highlight the salient features of the Scheme, have been reproduced from the Scheme, below.
Please note that the provisions reproduced below are not exhaustive and have been limited to key provisions, in the interest of
brevity. Please refer to the Scheme for detailed provisions.
Transfer and Vesting of the Demerged Undertaking
With effect from the Appointed Date, the Demerged Undertaking shall, in accordance with Section 2(19AA) and other applicable
provisions of the Income Tax Act and pursuant to Sections 230 to 232 and other applicable provisions of the Act, and pursuant
to the Sanction Order, without any further act, instrument or deed, be demerged from the Demerged Company and stand
transferred to and vested in or be deemed to be transferred to and vested in the Resulting Company as a going concern, so as
to become the business undertaking, assets, liabilities, properties, permits, contracts, right, title, interest and authorities of the
Resulting Company by virtue of operation of law or otherwise and in the manner provided in the Scheme.
Transfer and Vesting on Amalgamation of the Amalgamating Company
With effect from the Appointed Date and subject to the provisions of Part III of the Scheme and pursuant to the sanction of the
Scheme by the Tribunal or any other competent authority and pursuant to Sections 230 to 232 and other applicable provisions
of the Act, the Amalgamating Company shall stand amalgamated with the Amalgamated Company as a going concern and all
assets and liabilities of the Amalgamating Company shall, without any further act, instrument or deed, stand transferred to and
vested in or be deemed to have been transferred to and vested in the Amalgamated Company, so as to become on and from the
Appointed Date, the assets and liabilities of the Amalgamated Company by virtue of operation of law or otherwise, and in the
manner provided in the Scheme.
Consideration
For the Demerger:
In consideration of the transfer and vesting of the Demerged Undertaking from the Demerged Company to the Resulting
Company in terms of the Scheme, each shareholder of the Demerged Company whose name is recorded in the register of
members and records of the depository as a shareholder of the Demerged Company as on the Record Date shall be issued and
allotted 1 (one) share of the Resulting Company (face value of ` 2/- each fully paid up), for every 1 (one) share of the Demerged
Company (face value of ` 2/- each fully paid up) of the same class of shares outstanding and as held by such shareholder in
the Demerged Company, without any further application, act or deed (“Share Entitlement Ratio”). The shares issued by the
Resulting Company pursuant to Clause 17 of the Scheme are hereinafter referred to as “Resulting Company New Shares”. The
allotment of the Resulting Company New Shares shall not extinguish the shareholding of the shareholders of the Demerged
Company.
The Resulting Company New Shares to be issued by the Resulting Company, pursuant to Clause 17 in respect of any shares
of the Demerged Company which are held in abeyance under any provisions of Applicable Law including the provisions of
Section 126 of the Act or pursuant to any process /requirements before Appropriate Authority or which the Resulting Company
is unable to issue due to non-receipt of relevant approvals or due to Applicable Laws or for any other reason shall, pending
allotment or settlement of dispute by order of Tribunal or any court or otherwise, be held by the Resulting Company in escrow
or shall be dealt with and issued to the concerned shareholder as provided under the Applicable Law. It is hereby clarified with
respect to the existing 570 partly paid-up shares of the Demerged Company (wherein ` 1 is outstanding on 310 shares and
` 0.50 is outstanding on 260 shares, both of face value ` 2/- each), the Resulting Company shall issue 570 fully paid-up
Resulting Company New Shares, but shall keep such Resulting Company New Shares in abeyance/suspense account till such
time as the Demerged Company receives the balance amount towards calls-in-arrear pertaining to such partly paid shares and/
or receipt of the appropriate judicial/regulatory direction in respect thereof. In case of a forfeiture of the said partly paid -up
shares after the Record Date by the Demerged Company, the Resulting Company New Shares relating to such forfeited partly
paid shares shall stand cancelled and the corresponding equity share capital of the Resulting Company shall stand automatically
reduced without the requirements of any further consents or approvals. The Resulting Company New Shares to be issued by
virtue of the shares of the Demerged Company held in investor education protection fund shall be issued to investor protection
fund in favour of such shareholders of the Demerged Company. The Resulting Company Shares to be issued by virtue of the
shares of the Demerged Company held in any escrow created from time to time shall be issued to or such escrows in favour of
such shareholders of the Demerged Company.
All shares of the Resulting Company will be listed and/or admitted to trading on the BSE and NSE, which have nation-
wide trading terminals. The Resulting Company shall apply for listing of its shares on the BSE and NSE and enter into such
arrangements and give such confirmations and/or undertakings as may be necessary in accordance with Applicable Law for
the Resulting Company, including for seeking exemption from Rule 19(2)(b) of Securities Contracts (Regulation) Rules, 1957.
The shares of the Resulting Company shall remain frozen in the depositories system till listing and trading permission is given
by the designated Stock Exchange. There shall be no change in the shareholding pattern or control in the Resulting Company
between the Record Date and the listing which may affect the status of approvals received from the Stock Exchanges, other than

                                                                 66
as provided in the Scheme. The Resulting Company will not issue/reissue any shares, not covered under the Scheme, till the date
of listing of the Resulting Company on the BSE and NSE pursuant to the Scheme.
Prior to the issuance of the Resulting Company New Shares, the Resulting Company shall increase its authorised share capital,
if required so as to enable it to issue and allot the Resulting Company New Shares in the manner provided herein.
For the Amalgamation:
Since the Amalgamating Company is a wholly owned subsidiary of the Amalgamated Company with all shares in the share
capital of the Amalgamating Company being held by the Amalgamated Company, and the Amalgamated Company, being the
holding company, cannot issue or allot any shares to itself, no shares whatsoever shall be issued by the Amalgamated Company
in consideration of the amalgamation. Accordingly, all such shares of the Amalgamating Company held by the Amalgamated
Company and the investment of the Amalgamated Company in such shares as appearing in the books of the Amalgamated
Company shall stand cancelled upon the Scheme becoming effective without issue or allotment of new shares in lieu of shares
of the Amalgamating Company.
Name Change
Amalgamation: Upon the Scheme becoming effective and subject to Clause 41.3 of the Scheme, the name of the Amalgamated
Company or Demerged Company shall stand changed on and from the Effective Date to “TATA MOTORS PASSENGER
VEHICLES LIMITED” or such other name which is determined by the Board of the Amalgamated Company and no separate
act, procedure, instrument, or deed and registration fees shall be required to be followed under the Act.
Demerger: Upon the Scheme becoming effective and simultaneously with the change of name of the Amalgamated Company,
the name of our Company shall stand changed on and from the Effective Date to “TATA MOTORS LIMITED” or such other
name which is available and approved by the RoC, by filing the requisite forms with the Appropriate Authority and no separate
act, procedure, instrument, or deed and registration fees shall be required to be followed under the Act.
Employees
Demerger: All the Transferring Employees shall be deemed to have become employees of the Resulting Company on and
from the Effective Date, without interruption of service, on terms and conditions of employment no less favourable than those
applicable to them with reference to their employment in the Demerged Company. The Resulting Company shall abide by any
subsisting agreement / settlement, entered into by the Demerged Company with any of the Transferring Employees or employee
representative bodies / unions. The past services of all the Transferring Employees with the Demerged Company prior to the
demerger of the Demerged Undertaking into the Resulting Company, shall be taken into account for the purposes of all benefits
to which the Transferring Employees may be eligible, including for the purpose of payment of any retrenchment or redundancy
compensation, leave encashment, gratuity and other terminal benefits.
Amalgamation: All Amalgamating Company Employees shall be deemed to have become employees of the Amalgamated
Company on and from the Effective Date, without interruption of service, on terms and conditions of employment no less
favourable than those applicable to them with reference to their employment in the Amalgamated Company. The Amalgamated
Company undertakes to abide by any subsisting agreement/ settlement, entered into by the Amalgamating Company with any
of the Amalgamating Company Employees or employee representative bodies/ unions. The past services of all Amalgamating
Company Employees with the Amalgamating Company prior to the Effective Date shall be taken into account for the purposes
of all benefits to which the Amalgamating Company Employees may be eligible, including for the purpose of payment of any
retrenchment or redundancy compensation, leave encashment, gratuity and other terminal benefits.
Employee Stock Option Scheme
Upon the effectiveness of the Scheme, notwithstanding anything contained in the Demerged Company Incentive Scheme,
for every unexercised performance share unit (whether vested or not) outstanding and granted to the participants under the
Demerged Company Incentive Scheme(s) (“Participants”), as on the Record Date, such Participant shall be entitled to and be
granted 1 (one) performance share unit by the Resulting Company under a new incentive scheme.
The performance share units already granted by the Demerged Company under the Demerged Company Incentive Scheme
to the Participants would continue to be held by the Participants and, notwithstanding anything contained in the Demerged
Company Incentive Scheme, the vesting and exercise of the same shall take place as per (i) Clauses 11 to Clause 14 of Tata
Motors Limited Share based Long Term Incentive Scheme 2021, and (ii) Clauses 10 to Clause 13 of Tata Motors Limited Share
based Long Term Incentive Scheme 2024.
The Resulting Company shall take into account the period during which the Participants held the performance share units granted
by the Demerged Company prior to the issuance of the performance share units by the Resulting Company, for determining of
minimum vesting period/ exercise period required for performance share units, as the case may be, that may be granted by the
Resulting Company.

Legal Proceedings
For the Demerger:
Non Tax Proceedings
Upon the Scheme becoming effective, if any suit, appeal, legal, or other proceeding of whatever nature (excluding Tax
proceedings), whether criminal or civil (including before any statutory or quasi-judicial authority or tribunal), under Applicable
Law, by or against the Demerged Company in relation to the Demerged Undertaking is pending on the Effective Date or is
instituted any time thereafter, the same shall not abate or be discontinued or in any way be prejudicially affected by reason of
or by anything contained in the Scheme, but the said suit, appeal or other legal proceedings shall be continued, prosecuted and
enforced by or against the Resulting Company, as the case may be, after the Effective Date, in the same manner and to the same
extent as it would have been continued, prosecuted and enforced by or against the Demerged Company, as if the Scheme had
not been made
Direct Tax Litigations
The Demerged Company shall be liable for any tax payable to the Appropriate Authorities as per the applicable Direct Tax Laws
and shall be entitled to any refunds of tax from the Appropriate Authorities under the applicable Direct Tax Laws pertaining to
the period prior to the Appointed Date, regardless of whether such payments or receipts are provided or recorded in the books
of the Demerged Company and whether such payments or receipts are due or realised on, before or after the Appointed Date.
The Resulting Company shall be liable for any tax payable to the Appropriate Authorities under applicable Direct Tax Laws and
shall be entitled to refunds of any tax from the Appropriate Authorities under applicable Direct Tax Laws, which in each case,
arise from the operation or activities of the Demerged Undertaking on or after the Appointed Date, regardless of whether such
payments or receipts are provided or recorded in the books of the Demerged Company and whether such payments or receipts
are due or realised on or after the Appointed Date

Indirect Tax Litigations

civil (including before any statutory or quasi-judicial authority or tribunal), under applicable Indirect Tax Laws, by or against

time thereafter against the Demerged Company, and if such proceeding is capable of being continued by or against the Resulting
Company under Applicable Law, the same shall not abate or be discontinued or in any way be prejudicially affected by reason
of or by anything contained in the Scheme, but the said suit, appeal or other legal proceedings shall be continued, prosecuted
and enforced by or against the Resulting Company, as the case may be, after the Effective Date, in the same manner and to the
same extent as it would have been continued, prosecuted and enforced by or against the Demerged Company, as if the Scheme
had not been made.
For the Amalgamation:
If any suit, cause of actions, appeal or other legal, quasi-judicial, arbitral or other administrative proceedings, including Tax
assessment proceedings/appeals, of whatever nature (hereinafter called the “Proceedings of the Amalgamating Company’’)
by or against the Amalgamating Company are pending and/or arising on the Effective Date and relate to the Amalgamating
Company, the same shall not abate, be discontinued or be in any way prejudicially affected by reason of the amalgamation
or of anything contained in the Scheme, but the Proceedings of the Amalgamating Company may be continued, prosecuted
and enforced by or against the Amalgamated Company in the same manner and to the same extent as it would or might
have been continued, prosecuted and enforced by or against the Amalgamating Company as if the Scheme had not been
made. On and from the Effective Date, the Amalgamated Company may initiate any legal proceeding for and on behalf of the
Amalgamating Company. The Amalgamated Company undertakes to have all legal or other proceedings initiated by or against
the Amalgamating Company, which are capable of being continued by or against the Amalgamated Company, transferred to its
name as soon as is reasonably possible after the Effective Date and to have the same continued, prosecuted and enforced by or
against the Amalgamated Company.

Global Economy
According to the IMF World Economic Outlook, 2025(1), the global economy is projected to grow at 3.0% in 2025 as major
policy shifts are resetting the global trade system and giving rise to uncertainty that is once again testing the resilience of
the global economics. Signs of stabilization which had emerged through much of 2024 after prolonged and challenging
period of unprecedented shocks. However, the recent tariffs have given rise to uncertainty testing the resilience of the global
economy. Global inflation is expected to fall, but US inflation is predicted to stay above target. Downside risks from potentially
higher tariffs, elevated uncertainty, and geopolitical tensions persist.
Note: (1) World Economic Outlook, April 2025
Indian Economy
The International Monetary Fund (IMF) has projected India’s GDP growth at 6.4% in CY 2025(2). This forecast reflects
India’s strong, economic fundamentals and resilience amid global economic challenges. On the infrastructure front, India has
significantly ramped up its capital expenditure with increased Union budget allocation. For the fiscal year 2025-26, the Indian
government has set up capital expenditure (capex) at ` 11.21 lac crore, marking a 10.08% from the previous year’s revised
estimate.
Note: (2) https://www.imf.org/en/Publications/WEO/Issues/2025/07/29/world-economic-outlook-update-july-2025.
Segment Wise Structure of the Indian CV Industry
Heavy Commercial Vehicles (HCVs) – GVW > 16.2 Tonnes
HCVs form the backbone of long-haul freight and infrastructure logistics in India. This segment includes multi-axle rigid
trucks, tractor-trailers, and tippers. Key applications include long-haul cargo transport, mining, construction, and industrial
raw material movement. Customers are typically large fleet operators and contractors. Trends include increasing preference for
higher-tonnage vehicles, adoption of telematics, and demand for alternate fuel variants. The segment is also witnessing interest
in LNG and hydrogen-powered trucks for long-distance applications
Intermediate and Light Commercial Vehicles (ILCVs) – GVW 3.5 to 16.2 Tonnes
ILCVs serve regional and intra-city logistics needs. They are versatile, fuel-efficient, and suitable for medium-duty applications.
These typically include FMCG and e-commerce distribution, agro-produce transport, and courier services. Customers include
SMEs and owner-drivers. Trends include shift towards higher payload variants, increasing demand for CNG and electric ILCVs.
OEMs are introducing modular platforms and connected features to enhance value proposition.
Small Commercial Vehicles (SCVs) – GVW < 3.5 Tonnes
SCVs are widely used for last-mile delivery and rural transport. They include mini trucks, pickups and three wheelers.
Applications include market load operations, delivery of groceries, LPG, milk, e-commerce, and municipal services. Customers
are typically micro-entrepreneurs and aggregator platforms. Trends include electrification, shift towards CNG and bi-fuel
variants (especially in urban centres), new financing models prompted by emergence of startups and tech companies.

                                                                70
Buses – Passenger CVs (All GVW Ranges)
The bus segment includes vehicles used for public transport, school and staff commute, intercity travel, and tourism. Applications
include STU operations, educational institutions, and private fleet services. Customers include government transport corporations
and tour operators. Trends include increased shift towards CNG, strong policy push for electric buses, growing demand for
low-floor and AC buses, increased pull for passenger comfort features, and shift towards leasing and Own-Operate-Maintain
models (especially in EVs).
Global and Indian Commercial Vehicle Industry
The global commercial vehicle (CV) industry is undergoing a transformative shift, driven by megatrends such as electrification,
connectivity, autonomous technologies, and sustainability imperatives. Developed markets are witnessing accelerated adoption
of zero-emission vehicles, advanced driver assistance systems (ADAS), and digital fleet management solutions. Emerging
markets, while still dominated by internal combustion engine (ICE) platforms, are increasingly aligning with global trends
through regulatory reforms and infrastructure investments.
According to CRISIL ratings (2), Indian CV market volumes are expected to reach 1 million units in FY26, reclaiming their
pre-pandemic peak logged in 2019, growing at 3-5% in the current fiscal driven by revival in infrastructure spending which
gained momentum in Q4 FY25 and is likely to sustain on the back of 10-11% growth in central government capex. A strong
replacement demand cycle which accounts for 20% of the volume is expected further support demand.
LCV’s which account for 62% of the total volume are expected to grow by 4-6% driven by factors such as growing penetration of
e-commerce and warehousing while a pick-up in freight intensive sectors such as cement and mining will boost overall demand.
M&HCV volumes accounting for 30-35% of the total volumes are expected to grow at 2-4% this fiscal led by infrastructure
spending across construction, roads and metro rail projects. In the buses segment, the PM e-bus Sewa scheme launched in
August 2023 with an estimated cost of ` 57,613 cr aims to deploy 10,000 electric buses across 100 cities is expected to catalyse
demand.
Note: (2) https://www.crisilratings.com/en/home/newsroom/press-releases/2025/04/after-seven-years-cv-sales-to-drive-close-
to-one-million-milestone.html
Long Term Growth Drivers for the Indian CV Industry
Demand for CV is driven by the following factors:
Infrastructure Development: Government-led investments in highways, expressways, logistics parks, and smart cities
continue to drive demand for freight and passenger CVs. Execution momentum under programs like Bharatmala and Gati
Shakti are expected to sustain long-term growth. The expansion of industrial corridors and multimodal transport networks is
also contributing to increased CV utilization.
Urbanization and Mobility Needs: Rising urbanization and population density are increasing the need for efficient public
transport and last-mile connectivity, boosting demand for buses, vans, and small commercial vehicles. Smart city initiatives and
metro feeder services are creating new use cases for CVs, especially in the passenger segment.
E-commerce and Logistics Expansion: The rapid growth of e-commerce and organized retail has created new demand for
light and intermediate CVs, especially in urban and semi-urban areas. Warehousing and distribution networks are expanding,
requiring agile and efficient transport solutions.
Electrification and Sustainability Push: Regulatory incentives and state transport undertakings (STUs) are driving adoption
of electric buses and alternate fuel CVs, supported by growing ecosystem readiness. OEMs are investing in battery labs,
hydrogen ICE technology, and charging infrastructure to support this transition.
Replacement Demand and Fleet Modernization: Scrappage policies and tightening emission norms are encouraging fleet
replacement, particularly in urban centers and high-utilization segments. Fleet operators are upgrading to newer models with
better fuel efficiency, safety features, and digital capabilities.
Risks to Growth
Input Cost Volatility: Fluctuations in commodity prices and fuel costs can impact margins and customer affordability. Steel,
rubber, and semiconductor prices have shown volatility, affecting production costs.
Regulatory Uncertainty: Frequent changes in emission norms, safety standards, and taxation policies require agile compliance
and product adaptation. Uncertainty around implementation timelines can disrupt planning and investment cycles.
Financing Constraints: Limited access to affordable credit for small fleet operators and first-time buyers can dampen demand.
NBFCs and banks are tightening lending norms, impacting vehicle purchases.
Aggregator Disruption: Digital freight platforms offering low-cost services are challenging traditional transport models,
especially in SCV and ILCV segments. This is leading to margin pressure and changing customer acquisition dynamics.


                                                               71
Global Supply Chain Dependencies: Semiconductor shortages and import dependencies for EV components pose risks to
production continuity. OEMs are exploring localization strategies to mitigate these risks.
Diesel Blending Push: Isobutanol blending in Diesel, as announced by the Government of India, will present itself as a challenge
in terms of technological development, emissions compliance and may have some impact on overall cost of operations of all
commercial diesel vehicles. Policy transparency and a clear roadmap, price support and small scale pilots will play a critical
role to ensure this transition is managed smoothly for our customers.
Factors impacting demand for CV’s in India
Industrial Output and Construction Activity: Demand for HCVs and tippers is closely linked to mining, cement, and
infrastructure sectors. Government spending on capital projects directly impacts vehicle sales.
Seasonality and Monsoon Cycles: Agricultural cycles and monsoon intensity influence rural freight and passenger
movement. Demand for SCVs and pickups typically rises during harvest and festival seasons.
Fuel Price Trends: Diesel and CNG price movements directly affect operating economics and fleet utilization. Stable fuel
prices improve transporter profitability and encourage fleet expansion.
Policy and Tendering Activity: STU procurement cycles and government schemes (e.g., FAME) influence demand for buses
and electric CVs. Timely execution of tenders and subsidies is critical for sustained growth.
Review of Indian CV Industry and TMLCV’s Competitive Positioning
The Indian CV industry is segmented into HCVs, ILCVs, SCVs, and Buses, each catering to distinct use cases and customer
profiles. TMLCV maintains a leadership position across these segments through its robust product portfolio, technology
differentiation, and customer-centric approach.
In HCVs, the CV Business offers high-performance tractors, tippers, and cargo trucks suited for long-haul and industrial
applications. In ILCVs, the company provides fuel-efficient application focussed reliable vehicles for regional logistics. The
SCV segment is anchored by the widely recognized Ace and Yodha platforms, known for reliability and cost-effectiveness. This
range is now further augmented by Intra and AcePro platform. In the bus segment, TMLCV has a wide bus portfolio addressing
diverse segments and is a pioneer in electric buses and alternate fuel platforms, with strong order book visibility.
The CV Business’s competitive strengths include deep customer relationships, integrated service and parts ecosystem,
technology leadership in alternate fuels and connected vehicles, and strong brand equity supported by a pan-India network. The
company also benefits from its manufacturing scale, R&D capabilities, and strategic partnerships with suppliers and financiers.
Outlook for the CV Industry
The Indian CV industry is expected to maintain a steady growth trajectory, supported by macroeconomic stability, infrastructure
momentum, and technology adoption. Electrification, digitization, and sustainability will be key themes shaping future demand.
Recent reductions in GST are expected to improve cash flows and disposable incomes increasing demand for LCVs. Further,
GST reductions have lowered acquisition costs for LCVs and Pickups (<3.5 GW) making vehicles more accessible for cost
conscious buyers.
TMLCV is well-positioned to lead this transformation through its customer-centric approach, diversified portfolio, and
innovation capabilities. Continued investments in R&D, partnerships, and ecosystem development will enable the company to
capture emerging opportunities and strengthen its market leadership. The company is also exploring new business models such
as vehicle-as-a-service, digital marketplaces, and circular economy initiatives.

Overview
Our Company was incorporated as a public limited company under the Companies Act, 2013 with the name ‘TML Commercial
Vehicles Limited’ and a certificate of incorporation dated June 23, 2024 was issued by the Registrar of Companies. Pursuant
to the Scheme, fresh certificate of incorporation for change of name “TML Commercial Vehicles Limited” to “Tata Motors
Limited” was issued by Registrar of Companies on October 29, 2025.
Prior to the Scheme becoming effective, our Company was a wholly owned subsidiary of Tata Motors Limited. The main object
of our Company is to carry on the business of design, development, manufacturing and sale of commercial vehicles. Pursuant
to the Scheme becoming effective on October 1 2025, the CV Business of Tata Motors Limited has been demerged into and has
vested in our Company with effect from July 1, 2025 (i.e., the Appointed Date).
Our Commercial Vehicle Business is one of India’s leading CV manufacturers offering a wide range of products and services
portfolio catering to cargo and public mobility segments. We are engaged in the business of design, development, manufacturing
and distribution of commercial vehicles (SCVs and Pickups, Medium and Heavy Commercial Vehicles, Intermediate and Light
Commercial Vehicles and CV Passenger Vehicles) manufactured under the Tata and Daewoo brands along with associated
service, spare parts, digital and other related businesses. With the restructuring of our business into 8 focussed business
verticals now fully embedded, our transformation into a future ready, customer centric organization is enhancing our agility,
accountability and aligning us closely with our strategic priorities and the evolving needs of our customers.
Our Products Portfolio
1.   Trucks Business (MHCVs and ILCVs): We manufacture a variety of MHCVs and ILCVs, which include trucks, tractors,
     tippers, multi-axle vehicles and pickups with GVWs (including payload) of between 3.5 tons and 55 tons. We also provide
     fully built solutions for special applications like garbage compactors, containers, tankers, reefers, and diesel bowser to
     customers and various government organizations, including solutions related to national defense. In addition, through
     Tata Daewoo Mobility Limited, we manufacture a wide array of trucks ranging from 215 horsepower to 560 horsepower,
     including dump trucks, tractor trailers, mixers and cargo vehicles. Our signature product is the Prima range of trucks, which
     are sold in India and exported South Korea, as well as exported to a number of countries in South Asia, the Middle East
     and Africa. The SIGNA range of new MHCV trucks launched in 2016 has been extended to several additional tractor and
     tipper variants. Similarly, the newest addition to this portfolio—the Ultra range—now spans across multiple tonnage points
     starting from 5-ton Light Commercial Vehicles (“LCV”) to 30-ton tractors
2.   SCVs and Pickups: We manufacture a variety of small Commercial Vehicles and pickup trucks (less than 3.5 ton). This
     includes the Tata Ace, India’s first indigenously developed mini-truck, with a sub-1 ton payload with different fuel options
     (diesel, cng, gasolene, ev), the Tata Intra (V10,V20,V30,V50) with different payload options and the Tata Yodha pickup
     range with single cab and double cab variants and 4X2 and 4X4 options including the 2Ton payload variant.
3.   CV Passenger Vehicles (Buses and Smart Mobility Solutions): We manufacture a variety of passenger carriers, including
     buses. Our products include Magic Express, including an electric variant, a passenger variant for commercial transportation
     developed on the Tata Ace platform, and the Winger. We also offer a range of buses, which includes the Semi Deluxe
     Starbus Ultra Contract Bus and the new Starbus Ultra. Our range of buses is intended for a variety of uses, including
     as intercity coaches (with both air-conditioned and non-air-conditioned luxury variants), as school transportation and as
     ambulances. We also offer a range of electric buses in different configurations for every application. Additionally, our
     subsidiaries Tata Motors Body Solutions Limited and ACGL are engaged in the business of building bus bodies
4.   Digital Business (Fleet Edge and Freight Tiger):
     Our Commercial Business is aiming to redefine fleet and logistics management through its advanced digital platforms—
     Fleet Edge and Freight Tiger.
                                                               73
Fleet Edge is a telematics-based solution that enables real-time monitoring of vehicle health, driving behaviour, fuel
efficiency, and predictive maintenance across a vast connected fleet. It empowers fleet operators with actionable insights to
enhance uptime, reduce operating costs, and improve safety.
Freight Tiger offers intelligent logistics optimization, including smart routing, load matching, and end-to-end supply
chain visibility.
Together, these platforms create a seamless digital ecosystem that supports smarter decision-making and operational
efficiency. With AI-powered tools like Mileage Saarthi and integrated service features, Tata Motors is delivering a future-
ready, customer-centric experience for commercial mobility.
Our Product Range:




Tata Intra V70 Gold: Tata Intra V70 Gold showcases performance with a 2 tonne payload capacity.
Prima 4830.T: Prima 4830.T offers a state of the art ergonomic cabin and improved class features that aim to maximize
productivity and minimize driver fatigue.
Winger 9S: The Winger 9S aims to blend passenger comfort with operator friendly fuel.
Magic Bi-Fuel: Magic Bi-Fuel aims to lower ownership cost, and has value driven features, useful for student, staff and
last mile transport.
Sales and Service Network:
Our CV Business has an extensive sales and service network in the industry, ensuring seamless reach and support across
domestic and international markets. Domestically, the company operates through over 1,300 sales outlets and 3,200
service touchpoints, strategically located to serve urban, semi-urban, and rural customers efficiently. Internationally, our
Commercial Vehicle Business has a presence in over 40 countries, supported by a growing network of export dealerships
and service partners that cater to regional mobility needs. The service ecosystem includes Tata Authorized Service Stations,
spare parts distributors, retailers, and Customer Success Centres (CSCs) that offer live vehicle health monitoring and
proactive support. With over 800,000 connected vehicles on the Fleet Edge platform, our Commercial Vehicle Business
delivers predictive maintenance, uptime guarantees, and digital service access—enhancing customer experience and
operational efficiency. This robust infrastructure ensures reliable service and support throughout its lifecycle.
Insurance and Financing:
Our Commercial Vehicle business extends its customer-centric approach through dedicated operations in insurance broking
and vehicle financing. Insurance services are offered via Tata Motors Insurance Broking and Advisory Services Limited,
which aims to facilitate seamless access to motor insurance solutions tailored for commercial vehicle customers. On
the financing front, Tata Motors Finance Limited., a wholly owned step-down subsidiary, previously provided vehicle

                                                          74
     financing through independent dealers and a branch network. In FY25, this financing arm was merged into Tata Capital
     Ltd., following approvals from the National Company Law Tribunal and other regulatory bodies. The merger streamlines
     financing operations under Tata Capital, while Tata Motors Finance Holdings Ltd. and TMF Business Services Ltd. continue
     to support leasing and financing activities within the commercial vehicle segment.
Our Strategies
The CV industry is poised for technology enabled disruption across the globe as Connected CV’s become the industry norm for
delivering improved efficiency, de-carbonization from ICE to battery electric and hydrogen, integration of ADAS integration
leading to semi-autonomous driving and software led vehicle development for delivering greater customer value takes centre
stage.
Accordingly, our focus is on profitable leadership in mature markets and pursuing new growth areas such as New international
markets and non-cyclical revenue streams such as Downstream Business and Digital Business.




1.   Accelerating our digital business
     A core part of our long-term strategy is building a robust, digitally connected ecosystem that includes suppliers, channel
     partners, mechanics, fleet owners, logistics providers and importantly drivers. Fleet Edge, our advanced telematics-based
     platform now powers more than 8,00,000 vehicles delivering actionable insights to drivers and fleet owners. This has led
     to measurable improvements in operational efficiency and productivity. With strong renewal rate, the platform continues
     to expand its footprint. The integration of Mileage Saarthi, a machine learning powered tool, has further enhanced its
     value proposition – enabling upto 6% improvement in real world fuel economy. Our collaboration with Freight Tiger is
     set to deepen, with a clear focus on scaling subscriber growth, enriching solution offerings, driving higher levels of active
     engagement.
     FleetVerse, our comprehensive and innovate digital marketplace for Tata Motors Commercial Vehicles, offers a seamless
     experience across vehicle discovery, configuration, acquisition and financing. Designed to be future-ready, it evolving into
     a one stop digital destination for all commercial vehicle needs. The platform has now grown to a robust 4,37,000 users and
     45,062 retail partners with 15% of total retail transactions now routed through it.




                                                               75
2.   Expanding our development business
     The Downstream Business has five consecutive years of recorded growth in spares and service penetration while also
     expanding into new areas such as Tata Motors Automotive Fluids (TMAF), Aggregates and Fleet Care. E-Dukaan, the
     digital platform for genuine spare parts and automotive fluids, registered 47% year on year growth in FY25. We intend to
     expand our Downstream Business through:
     a.   Portfolio Competitiveness: Improved price positioning in service parts and develop new products to serve evolving
          customer needs
     b.   Supply Excellence: End to end digitally enabled supply chain and consumption led fulfillment
     c.   Channel Effectiveness: Expand Network and improve its effectiveness and profitability and new models for customer
          outreach and engagement
d.   Digital Footprint efficiency: Digital Ecosystem offering a seamless customer experience




3.   Continued focus on innovation and new product development
     Addressing the evolving needs of our customers across various segments, our Commercial Vehicle Business continues to
     enhance its comprehensive range of commercial cargo and passenger transport vehicles. Its approach has always been to
     consider regulatory change as a value enhancement opportunity for customers. Its commitment is to deliver total cost of
     ownership, higher vehicle uptime and value added services that enhance customer productivity and operational efficiency.
     During Financial Year 2025, the Commercial Vehicle business made significant strides in product and technology leadership.
     Our Commercial Vehicle Business became the first Indian Commercial Vehicle manufacturer for ADAS Level II, marking
     a key milestone in intelligent mobility. Reinforcing our focus on sustainable transportation, we initiated the first ever trials
     of hydrogen powered heavy trucks in India. Additionally, we achieved full compliance with AIS:29 revised standards,
     significantly enhancing truck cabin safety and ensuring greater occupant protection in line with evolving regulatory
     requirements. These achievements underscore our commitment to innovation, safety and environmental responsibility.
     Our Commercial Vehicle business continues to invest in EV, CNG, LNG and hydrogen ensuring that customers have
     a range of sustainable choices. Our Commercial Vehicle Business has invested ahead of time in various EV hardware
     aggregates as well as control software which will enhance the performance and efficiency of our elective vehicles being
     launched across the range during the year. Similarly, the Commercial Vehicle Business is actively exploring opportunities
     in software defined vehicles, including enabling vehicle architecture and technology stack with an aim to address India-
     specific market and customer requirements.
4.   Embracing Digital and AI opportunity in Operations
     The digital foundations laid over the past years are now enabling us to adopt AI-led transformations-both in customer facing
     solutions and internal operations. Our Commercial Vehicle Business is piloting AI driven predictive maintenance, real time
     fleet insights, intelligent CRM tools and personalisation in sales journeys. These steps will help us offer differentiated
     value, sharpen our responsiveness and elevate user experience.

     Our Commercial Vehicle Business has successfully deployed Industry 4.0 across seven strategic themes driving measurable

Plant Locations and Installed Capacity, Capacity Utilization in FY25 for the Demerged Undertaking:
We operate five principal automotive manufacturing facilities in India. The first facility was established in 1945 at Jamshedpur in
the state of Jharkhand in eastern India. We commenced construction of the second facility in 1966 (with production commencing
in 1976) at Pune, in the state of Maharashtra in western India, the third facility in 1985 (with production commencing in 1992)
at Lucknow, in the state of Uttar Pradesh in northern India, the fourth at Pantnagar in the state of Uttarakhand, India, which
commenced operations in Fiscal 2008, and the fifth facility for manufacturing of buses and LCVs at Dharwad in Karnataka
(which buses are also produced at Lucknow). The Jamshedpur, Pune, Pantnagar and Lucknow manufacturing facilities have
been accredited with an ISO/TS 16949:2000(E) certification.

Manufacturing Process and Technology
In FY25, our Commercial Vehicle Business expanded the adoption of Industry 4.0 technologies across its production facilities.
The unit has initiated adoption of SAP S/4HANA to establish a futureready, digitally native ERP platform. Advanced computer
vision and machine learning systems are deployed on the shop floor to proactively identify quality deviations across painting,
casting, and assembly processes. Predictive analytics tools monitor sealant gaps, paint thickness, and structural welds, ensuring
superior firsttimeright outcomes. Safety has been bolstered through realtime video analytics that detect PPE noncompliance,
restricted zone access, and operator fatigue. These AIled interventions have strengthened shopfloor safety governance across
all plants.
Our Suppliers
Our Commercial Vehicle Business maintains a robust and diversified supplier network that plays a critical role in delivering
quality, reliable and innovative mobility solutions. The supplier ecosystem spans across categories including aggregates, spare
parts & fluids, and re-manufactured parts & aggregates, supporting both ICE and electric vehicle platforms. Our Commercial
Vehicle Business integrates sustainability and performance into its sourcing strategy, working closely with suppliers to ensure
compliance with applicable regulatory standards, quality benchmarks, and cost efficiency. Through structured engagement,
supplier assessments, and collaborative development programs, our Commercial Vehicle Business fosters long-term
partnerships that enable agile, innovative, resilient and Atmanirbhar value chain. This ecosystem aims to support the company’s
transformation towards new technologies, viz alternate fuels, electrification and sustainability goals.
R&D
Our Commercial Vehicle Business with a long-term vision has been committed to sustainability of mobility solutions. Our CV
Business’s Engineering Research Centre (ERC) has been investing into development of new technologies and products. Led
with investments into people and infrastructure interwoven with a robust framework of processes, our CV Business has been
demonstrating innovation and advanced research across its product & logistics portfolio.
The CV Business R&D strategy has been focused towards developing advanced technologies, commensurate to the need for
energy security, decarbonization, regulatory environment, technology disruptions, evolving customer choices and increased
self-reliance. The R&D efforts span across products, services, and the extended ecosystem i.e., from the long living traditional
fuel based internal combustion engine technologies to new energy propulsion systems like Batteries, Hydrogen fuel cell and
Hydrogen ICE; from basic infotainment to high speed connected vehicle features and Advanced Driver Assistance Systems
(ADAS).
Our Commercial Vehicle Business leverages its state-of-the-art assets like the advanced powertrain centre, battery development
lab, power electronics lab, digital product development lab, materials lab, component testing rigs, test tracks, integrated safety
lab and associated utilities, for enabling the design, development, validation of technologies and products. The R & D efforts
are also complemented with long standing collaborations with technology partners and institutions of global repute, which
strengthen our competencies. With a growing emphasis on software dependence, our CV Business’s R&D initiatives are shaping
the future of commercial transportation—delivering cleaner, and efficient solutions for global markets.

Awards
Our Commercial Vehicle Business has earned widespread recognition for its innovation, sustainability, and safety initiatives.
In FY25, the CV Business was honored with the prestigious Golden Peacock Eco-Innovation Award for the Tata Ace EV and
received multiple Apollo Commercial Vehicle Awards 2024 across categories. Our Commercial Vehicle Business was also
acknowledged by SAE India Foundation for its corporate association and by CII for excellence in digitalization, robotics
automation, and sustainable material solutions. The Prima – Safe and Smart Truck received the Jury Mention Award at the
FICCI Road Safety Awards 2024, reinforcing the brand’s commitment to road safety. Additionally, the CV Business secured
four awards at the Intrapreneurship Conclave (Vanguard Awards) and was declared a winner at Asia IP Elite 2024 during the IP
Business Congress in Tokyo. These accolades reflect our Commercial Vehicle business’s leadership in delivering future-ready,
customer-centric, and environmentally responsible mobility solutions.
Corporate Social Responsibility
Our CV Business is committed to driving sustainable mobility through focused actions across three pillars: net-zero emissions,
circular economy, and biodiversity preservation. The company has pledged to achieve net-zero emissions by 2045 and 100%
renewable electricity usage in operations by 2030. In FY25, our CV Business achieved 45% renewable energy penetration,
reduced Scope 3 emissions by 12%, and made three of its plants water-neutral and zero waste to landfill. Circularity is
embedded through initiatives like remanufacturing, refurbishing, and recycling of vehicle components, alongside advanced
battery recycling programs. On the CSR front, in FY25, our CV Business impacted over 14.78 lakh beneficiaries through 116
projects with a total spend of ₹140 crore. These initiatives span health, education, employability, and environmental protection,
reinforcing the company’s commitment to inclusive growth and community resilience
Intellectual Property
Our Commercial Vehicle Business creates, owns, and maintains a wide array of intellectual property assets throughout the
world that are among our most valuable assets. Our intellectual property assets include patents, trademarks, copyrights, designs,
trade secrets and other intellectual property rights. We proactively and aggressively seek to protect our intellectual property in
India and other countries. We have been granted 250 patents, 242 designs and 231 copyrights in India and 18 patents, 13 designs
in foreign jurisdictions and have 493 applications pending for registration of patents, designs and copyright registration in India
as well as other countries.
Additionally, our business holds a trademark portfolio of 156 Registered Trademarks and 29 Trademarks pending registration
in India, and 144 Registered Trademarks and 32 Trademarks pending registrations in various international jurisdictions outside
India. These trademarks are for our vehicle models and other promotional initiatives. Our Commercial Vehicle Business uses
the Tata brand, through a Brand Equity and Brand Promotion Agreement entered into with Tata Sons Private Limited. We
believe that establishment of the TATA word mark and logo mark in India and around the world is material to our operations.
As part of our acquisition of TDCV, we have rights to the perpetual and exclusive use of the Daewoo brand and trademarks in
South Korea and overseas markets for the product range of TDCV
IT Data Protection and Data Security
Our CV Business maintains a robust governance framework to safeguard its intellectual property and digital assets. The
company’s Intellectual Property Rights (IPR) systems are integrated into lifecycle management platforms, enabling structured
registration, tracking, and protection of proprietary innovations across business units. In parallel, our CV Business enforces a
comprehensive Data Classification Policy that categorizes information into Public, Internal, Confidential, and Sensitive tiers,
ensuring appropriate access controls and handling procedures for each level. This policy is supported by detailed procedures for
information asset identification, labeling, and exception handling, all managed by the IT Security team. To further strengthen
data protection, Tata Motors has rolled out awareness programs such as the Digital Personal Data Protection (DPDP) initiative,
promoting compliance with emerging privacy regulations and reinforcing employee accountability. These measures collectively
reflect Our Commercial Vehicle Business’s commitment to operational integrity, regulatory compliance, and the responsible
stewardship of its intellectual and digital resources
